<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14576452455388431399"><p> <strong>What's the big deal?</strong> </p><p>Unlike a lot of people, Matt Beckford is actually looking forward to turning thirty. His twenties really weren't so great...and now he has his love life, his career, his finances -- even his record collection -- pretty much in order, like any good grown-up should. But when, out of the blue, Elaine announces she "can't do this anymore," Matt is left wi</p></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14576452455388431399"><p>
  <strong>What's the big deal?</strong>
</p><p>Unlike a lot of people, Matt Beckford is actually looking forward to turning thirty. His twenties really weren't so great...and now he has his love life, his career, his finances -- even his record collection -- pretty much in order, like any good grown-up should. But when, out of the blue, Elaine announces she "can't do this anymore," Matt is left with the prospect of facing the big three-oh alone. Compounding his misery is the fact that he has to move back in with his parents.</p><p>
  <strong>What's it all about, Alfie?</strong>
</p><p>Mum and Dad immediately start driving Matt up the wall, and emails from Elaine and nights out with his old school chum Gershwin aren't enough to snap Matt out of his existential funk. So he decides to track down more old schoolmates and see how they're handling this thirty thing. One by one, he gets in touch with the rest of the magnificent seven -- Pete, Bev, Katrina, Elliot, and Ginny, his former on-off girlfriend -- and soon the old gang is back together. But they're a lot older and a lot has changed and, even if he and Ginny still seem attracted to each other, you can't have an on-off girlfriend when you're thirty. Can you?</p></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14576452455388431399">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

      <a href="/user/show/82567-rebekah" class="user" title="rebekah">rebekah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/469920.Turning_Thirty" title="Paperback 9780743477659" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">dick lit lovers, people turning 30</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer8798634">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2671951752674501134">I accidently stayed up all night reading this male alternative to chick lit, dick lit,(I think I made that genre up but it exsists we just call it fiction)anyway, I read it in one go not cuz it was so good but because in 6 months I too, will be turning thirty and my anxiety about this milestone in life kept me up and kept me reading. <br /><br />Have you ever been out with your boyfriend/girlfriend and their old school friends? And all they talk about is remember so and so? And whatever happened to...? And</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2671951752674501134">I accidently stayed up all night reading this male alternative to chick lit, dick lit,(I think I made that genre up but it exsists we just call it fiction)anyway, I read it in one go not cuz it was so good but because in 6 months I too, will be turning thirty and my anxiety about this milestone in life kept me up and kept me reading. <br /><br />Have you ever been out with your boyfriend/girlfriend and their old school friends? And all they talk about is remember so and so? And whatever happened to...? And it's really boring for you cuz you don't know those people and you don't care...And those HILARIOUS stories barely elicit a polite titter from you? That is what this book was like for me, it had a few light enjoyable moments and if I was drunk I might have found it more amusing. But it struck the freaking-out-about-turning-30 chord in me so I gave it two stars cuz I could relate and it helped me get through the night. I like when books can be my friend even if they are kind of a lame friend. </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13228175170692566861">The characters were so flat and unrealistic.       <a href="/user/show/32669562-thomas-str-mquist" class="user" title="Thomas Strömquist">Thomas Strömquist</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2185322.Turning_Thirty" title="Paperback 9780340792650" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/32669562-thomas-str-mquist?shelf=book-collection" class="actionLinkLite">book-collection</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer984148589">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3330758889910905162">In the genre he writes, this is a perfect one from Mike Gayle. With regards to his previous outings, the major difference is that he presents a protagonist in this one who is not a lazy whiner, but a most regular guy that you actually can relate to.<br /><br />Close to his 30th, Matt finds that he and his girlfriend really drifted apart and when she breaks the subject, it becomes one of these very admirable break-ups, where the parties really stay friends. Matt moves home (from the states) to mum and dad in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3330758889910905162">In the genre he writes, this is a perfect one from Mike Gayle. With regards to his previous outings, the major difference is that he presents a protagonist in this one who is not a lazy whiner, but a most regular guy that you actually can relate to.<br /><br />Close to his 30th, Matt finds that he and his girlfriend really drifted apart and when she breaks the subject, it becomes one of these very admirable break-ups, where the parties really stay friends. Matt moves home (from the states) to mum and dad in Birmingham, on his way to his newly acquired position in Australia. The good news is of course that he managed to stay close friend with his ex, the bad is that he realizes he's very much alone and with every outlook of being so for his 30th. Being on the home turf, he decides to say hello to the old gang.<br /><br />This is superbly written, balancing a nice humour and amusing situations on the right side of plausible. Gayle also presents a great cast of characters that is easy to relate to; daydreaming, going to sleep or waking up, I caught myself wondering about "whatever became of..." for some fractions of a second until I realized who I was thinking of.<br /><br />The other thing this book made me realize is that 40 really must be the new 30, considering I could relate so closely with the cast of the book turning 30. Or it could be that 45 is the new senile I suppose. Either way, this was wonderfully nostalgic and comes very highly recommended!</span>

      <a href="/user/show/9190824-sophie-blogger" class="user" title="Sophie (Blogger)">Sophie (Blogger)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/469920.Turning_Thirty" title="Paperback 9780743477659" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer886927683">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer994734568472016602">Turning Thirty is a big event in most people's lives, Matt is no different. Turning Thirty is a book about having everything you could ever want, and then losing it in a blink of an eye. After, Matt's life takes a turn for the worse leaving him no choice but to move back in with his parents. With no girlfriend or house, he doesn't know where his life went wrong. <br /><br />So, Matt decides to look towards the past instead of the future, finding his old school friends seems like a great idea being able to r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText994734568472016602">Turning Thirty is a big event in most people's lives, Matt is no different. Turning Thirty is a book about having everything you could ever want, and then losing it in a blink of an eye. After, Matt's life takes a turn for the worse leaving him no choice but to move back in with his parents. With no girlfriend or house, he doesn't know where his life went wrong. <br /><br />So, Matt decides to look towards the past instead of the future, finding his old school friends seems like a great idea being able to reflect on the good old times and not think about his looming 30th birthday. Over the remaining day left before he turns thirty, Matt comes to realise what is really means to turn thirty and how sometime you need the help of your oldest friends to make you see.<br /><br />With its entertaining theme it is a great book for any person to read but if you are close to or just turned Thirty then this book will make you see witty side of hitting the big 3-0. Turning Thirty shows that life doesn't end at thirty, it shows that life really starts at thirty, just like in Matt's case. He had lost everything, but he gain much more, his friends came back into his life and he realised that it is never to late to change your life.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="994734568472016602">...more</a>

          </span>

      <a href="/user/show/5527647-rise" class="user" title="Rise">Rise</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer178332560">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14531743655900362961">Dibeli karena mendadak galau karena keluyuran sendirian di toko buku (oke, kapan sih gw nggak galau?) dan juga terpengaruh obrolan soal rencana hidup bertemakan turning 25 dengan si BlaBla (yang akan berumur 25 tahun ini) sebelumnya. Jadi meskipun gw masih *cough* jauh dari usia 30, maka gw memutuskan untuk membeli buku ini.<br /><br />Dari segi cerita mungkin mirip chick lit ya, bedanya penulis dan tokoh utamanya pria. Plot utama berkisar pada kegalauan Matthew Beckford dalam menghadapi pergantian usia men</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14531743655900362961">Dibeli karena mendadak galau karena keluyuran sendirian di toko buku (oke, kapan sih gw nggak galau?) dan juga terpengaruh obrolan soal rencana hidup bertemakan turning 25 dengan si BlaBla (yang akan berumur 25 tahun ini) sebelumnya. Jadi meskipun gw masih *cough* jauh dari usia 30, maka gw memutuskan untuk membeli buku ini.<br /><br />Dari segi cerita mungkin mirip chick lit ya, bedanya penulis dan tokoh utamanya pria. Plot utama berkisar pada kegalauan Matthew Beckford dalam menghadapi pergantian usia menuju 30 tahun. Menurutnya, umur 30 tahun adalah saat aneka kegalauan usia duapuluhan berakhir dan hidup mulai berjalan dengan lancar, seperti misalnya memiliki aparetemen berwarna monokrom, rak anggur yang lengkap, dan yang paling penting, pasangan hidup. Sayangnya hal itu tidak terjadi, karena yang terjadi adalah Matt putus dengan pacarnya, meninggalkan apartemennya, pindah kerja (yang masih akan dimulai tiga bulan lagi), dan terpaksa tinggal di rumah orang tuanya. Dari sini, berbagai persoalan (dan kegalauan) mulai bermunculan kembali.<br /><br />Meskipun sebenernya novel semacam begini adalah yang biasanya nggak gw lirik, secara mengejutkan gw suka dengan novel ini. Tidak ada konflik yang benar-benar meningkat dan banyak kemunculan karakter di sana sini terkadang terasa membingungkan karena lebih tampil sebagai pemanis saja. Tapi dialog yang ada terasa menyenangkan untuk diikuti. Lumayan untuk mengisi waktu luang sembari mikir mau jadi apa pas udah berusia 30 nanti :)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14531743655900362961">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1171167231">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171167231" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/36412681-soho-black" class="left imgcol" title="Soho_black"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Soho_black" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1171167231?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/36412681-soho-black" class="user" title="Soho_black">Soho_black</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/469920.Turning_Thirty" title="Paperback 9780743477659" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/36412681-soho-black?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/36412681-soho-black?shelf=used-to-own" class="actionLinkLite">used-to-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1171167231">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17868498407488641926">30 is one of those funny ages, where you can still be told “oh, you’re still young” by people who have reached it, but where teenagers and people in their early 20s can make you feel dreadfully old. 30 is also one of those ages you use as a deadline. When you’re young, it seems so far away and so adult that you can safely say “I’ll do this by the time I’m 30”, knowing you have plenty of time. But as that deadline grows nearer, you wonder if your life is what it’s all made out to be.<br /><br />I’d had a cop</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17868498407488641926">30 is one of those funny ages, where you can still be told “oh, you’re still young” by people who have reached it, but where teenagers and people in their early 20s can make you feel dreadfully old. 30 is also one of those ages you use as a deadline. When you’re young, it seems so far away and so adult that you can safely say “I’ll do this by the time I’m 30”, knowing you have plenty of time. But as that deadline grows nearer, you wonder if your life is what it’s all made out to be.<br /><br />I’d had a copy of Mike Gayle’s “Turning Thirty” for a while, as I’d heard good things about his writing and had found a cheap 2nd hand copy. But it was only as that venerable age approached that I decided I’d perhaps best give it a read. After all, I didn’t know what 30 had in store, and could do with a little help. So, the week before the big day, I started taking it to work to read on the bus, joking with colleagues that it was my instruction manual for the big day.<br /><br />What a mistake that turned out to be!<br /><br />Matt Beckford is looking forward to turning thirty. He set up his goals for that birthday years ago and, as it approaches, he has the life he always wanted. He has a decent career, a wonderful partner and he’s going to be spending his 30th birthday in New York, and not his home town of Birmingham which, for Matt, is the ideal situation.<br /><br />Of course, nothing goes to way you plan it. 6 months before the big day, his girlfriend decides they should go their separate ways. This, because they’re living together in New York, and it’s her town rather than his, begins a series of changes. To assist the parting, he asks for a transfer away from New York and heads back to Birmingham to stay with his parents for a while before moving on again to his new job. Unfortunately for Matt, this means he’ll be spending his 30th birthday in his home town, without his ideal job and without a girlfriend. Indeed, without all the things that threatened to make turning thirty bearable in the first place.<br /><br />Returning home, Matt starts trying to get his old group of friends together again, despite having not seen any of them for a number of years. He discovers that whilst everyone had their dreams at thirteen, no two people’s lives are the same all those years on. Many have jobs; some of them even the job they wanted. Some have married and have children. And one, as they discover to their sadness, will never turn thirty, having died some years before.<br /><br />What potentially sets Mike Gayle apart from a lot of the other writers working in the chick- and bloke-lit genres at the moment is that he’s still in touch with reality. A lot of the situations in “Turning Thirty” could really happen to any of us. It’s maybe a little unlikely that all of them would happen to the same person and certain things, especially the ease with which he manages to track down his old friends and how easily their relationship seems to slip back into focus as if they’d never lost touch, are a little unrealistic, but by and large, this is real life. Whilst you can’t see yourself in the scene, you do care a little about the characters and, more importantly, you want to know what’s going to happen next. It’s a little like watching the soaps on TV. You know it’s not really life, but it’s near enough to keep you involved.<br /><br />Gayle’s writing style helps out a lot here, as well. He writes with a kind of easy, laid back style that mirrors the pace of many of our lives, particularly when they’re in a hiatus, like Matt’s is. Somehow, though, it’s tough to take your eyes away from. Again like the soaps, you know that something is likely to happen fairly soon but, unlike some of them, it’s easy enough on the eye that you keep going with it.<br /><br />However, for all its good points, reading “Turning Thirty” depressed me. As Matt observes in the book, “I think the art of taking [turning 30] well is being happy with what you’ve got”. Reading this when I did, a few days before I was thirty, and not being entirely happy with my lot, made it depressing. I was a little too involved in the story, not for the sake of the story, but for how it compared to my own life. Sadly, my own life didn’t match up to Matt’s, despite the situation he found himself in and that proved highly depressing. Had I read the book four years ago, when it was first published, I think I might have appreciated it a lot better.<br />This may not be the case for everyone, however. If you’re outside the 25-35 age range, this will be an amusing look forwards, or backwards, to that age where everything should be settled by. For the over 30s it may act as reminiscence, for the under 30s, it may be motivational, as I don’t think any of us want to celebrate our 30th birthday and then go back to our mother’s.<br /><br />If you’re within that age range, you need to think carefully before you read this. If life has turned out the way you hoped it would, then read this book. It’ll be a light hearted read about other people’s lives. With the broad range of characters and how their lives have turned out, there’s a pretty fair chance you’ll recognise yourself in here somewhere, which is never a bad thing. Even if there isn’t, it’s a pretty good read anyway.<br /><br />If you’re anything like me, however, and want more, or different, from what you have at 30, then stay clear. There is no catharsis here, just the realisation that even when a fictional character loses all he has; he still manages to have a more fulfilling time that you’re having. It’s a depressing experience, and you’d be far better off reading about someone blessed with luck even worse than your own.<br /><br />But when you reach 35, or when you are in a situation where you’re happy with what you have, by all means come back and have a read. Depressing though it may be if read at the wrong time, it’s still an easy, enjoyable novel. It’s not Mike Gayle’s fault that I happened to pull this book off my shelf at potentially the worst possible moment for it and I can see this is something I would have enjoyed immensely at any other time.<br /><br />Incidentally, if you’re around 30 and you don’t think you could stand the hurt this book may cause you, I can recommend Mike Gayle’s others. Despite what he’s done to me of late, he’s quite possibly the best bloke-lit author I’ve read, with a lightness of touch and a feeling of reality that Hornby and Parsons seem to lack. Give him a chance, as even I can see that he didn’t depress me on purpose, it just happened that way.<br /><br />This review may also appear under my name at any or all of <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.ciao.co.uk" target="_blank">www.ciao.co.uk</a>, <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.thebookbag.co.uk" target="_blank">www.thebookbag.co.uk</a>, <a href="http://www.goodreads.com" target="_blank">www.goodreads.com</a>, <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.co.uk" target="_blank">www.amazon.co.uk</a> and <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.dooyoo.co.uk" target="_blank">www.dooyoo.co.uk</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17868498407488641926">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1098893699">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1098893699" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/21675053-sharon" class="left imgcol" title="Sharon"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Sharon" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1098893699?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21675053-sharon" class="user" title="Sharon">Sharon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2185321.Turning_Thirty" title="Paperback 9780340767948" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1098893699">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13611498872757005426">I nearly didn’t bother with anymore Mike Gayle after the To Do List but thought I’d give one of his novels a go – and I’m really glad I did. This was miles better – a really thoughtful, philosophical book about growing up, looking back and trying to move forward in an unpredictable world. The main character Matt thinks he’s got his life planned out living in New York, good job and nice girlfriend, until one day they mutually decide that although they care deeply about each other they just are no</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13611498872757005426">I nearly didn’t bother with anymore Mike Gayle after the To Do List but thought I’d give one of his novels a go – and I’m really glad I did. This was miles better – a really thoughtful, philosophical book about growing up, looking back and trying to move forward in an unpredictable world. The main character Matt thinks he’s got his life planned out living in New York, good job and nice girlfriend, until one day they mutually decide that although they care deeply about each other they just are not ‘the one’ they each want to settle down with. So Matt’s life is instantly thrown into upheaval. He’s offered a job in Australia, but it doesn’t start for three months so he decides to go home to Birmingham and move back in with his parents for a while. But this throws up all kinds of weird and wonderful memories and Matt begins to question what happiness in life is really all about. I think they loosely call this kind of writing lad-lit but I actually enjoyed the writing style a lot more than some of the chick-lit I have read. The ending wasn’t predictable, I really cared for the characters and, written in the first person and in a very philosophical way, I kept forgetting that I wasn’t reading something autobiographical. Definitely recommend Turning Thirty to both men and women. I’m glad I wasn’t put off by The To Do List and I think I’ll give another of his novels a go. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13611498872757005426">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer927330732">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14039855340591878176"><br /><br />I admit it – I will be turning 30 soon myself (oh crikey) so Mike Gayle’s hilarious and poignant novel about a man who evaluates his life before the big day to find that maybe not everything is quite in order really hit home for me.<br />Where did you think you’d be when you turned 30? Top of the career ladder? In a swanky house, married with kids? Having split up with his girlfriend and forced to move back home, Matt Beckford is certain that being single and living with his parents in Birmingham wasn</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14039855340591878176"><br /><br />I admit it – I will be turning 30 soon myself (oh crikey) so Mike Gayle’s hilarious and poignant novel about a man who evaluates his life before the big day to find that maybe not everything is quite in order really hit home for me.<br />Where did you think you’d be when you turned 30? Top of the career ladder? In a swanky house, married with kids? Having split up with his girlfriend and forced to move back home, Matt Beckford is certain that being single and living with his parents in Birmingham wasn’t entirely the life his teenage self aspired to for this milestone and it’s making him nostalgic for simpler times. So Matt is determined to reunite with his old schoolmates – and as he does he discovers that life rarely turns out the way you planned.<br />I love Gayle’s conversational writing style – it makes me want to go to the pub and have a drink and a chat with him. But underneath that approachable humour he’s very good at pinpointing human behaviour in a way that’s quite tender and often wistfully accurate. His depiction of modern relationships is spot on and I have every faith that this book will appeal to men and women alike. And now I feel fully prepared for leaving my twenties behind. Kinda.<br /><br />Review by Nikki Mason on behalf of BestChapLit.com</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14696916573482034634">Category: Books<br /><br />Author: Mike Gayle<br /><br />Genre: Pop Literature<br /><br />Rate: 3 out of 5<br /><br />Buku yang gw dapatkan dari diskonan Gramedia di Lotte Mart Fatmawati. Alasan gw beli buku ini?<br /><br />1. Karena lagi diskon (cuma jadi 20 ribu, hehehe),<br /><br />2. Karena judulnya, Turning Thirty - Beranjak Tiga Puluh.<br /><br />Itulah kondisi gw sekarang.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText14696916573482034634">Category: Books<br /><br />Author: Mike Gayle<br /><br />Genre: Pop Literature<br /><br />Rate: 3 out of 5<br /><br />Buku yang gw dapatkan dari diskonan Gramedia di Lotte Mart Fatmawati. Alasan gw beli buku ini?<br /><br />1. Karena lagi diskon (cuma jadi 20 ribu, hehehe),<br /><br />2. Karena judulnya, Turning Thirty - Beranjak Tiga Puluh.<br /><br />Itulah kondisi gw sekarang. Beranjak tiga puluh. Saat gw menuliskan blog review ini, umur gw sama persis kayak Matt Beckford sang tokoh utama buku ini, yaitu 29 tahun.<br /><br />Matt Beckford adalah seorang programer komputer asal Birmingham, Inggris yang sukses. Di umurnya yang ke-29, ia mempunyai karir yang baik di New York, Amerika Serikat, juga punya pacar bernama Elaine yang seru. Namun semuanya berubah ketika Elaine bilang kalau ia sudah tidak mencintai Matt lagi. Apakah Matt sedih? Ternyata tidak, ia pun merasakan hal yang sama dengan Elaine. Mereka berdua merasa hubungan yang mereka jalani sudah hilang gregetnya. Matt dan Elaine pun berpisah baik-baik. Matt mengajukan permohonan untuk pindah cabang kantor. Permohonannya disetujui dan ia akan pindah ke cabang di Australia. Sebelum pindah ke tempat baru, Matt minta cuti sekitar tiga bulan yang ia gunakan untuk pulang ke rumah orang tuanya di Birmingham. Masa-masanya di kampung halaman ia gunakan untuk bertemu dengan teman-teman lamanya sambil terus mencari tahu apa artinya memasuki usia dekade ketiga.<br /><br />Secara garis besar, buku ini mengungkapkan pemikiran dan kebingungan orang-orang seumuran gw secara jujur dan lugas. Entah tentang kekagetan kita begitu menyadari hal-hal yang kita anggap keren itu udah lamaaaaa banget, kemunduran stamina fisik, fakta-fakta pertemanan yang akan dihadapi oleh orang-orang di akhir 20-an, pemikiran yang semakin hari semakin dalam, sampai berbagai pencapaian hidup yang kita pikir akan didapatkan.<br /><br />Gw membaca buku di umur yang tepat. Makanya gw bisa membaca buku ini dengan nrimo dan santai. Karena gw bisa mengerti tentang segala konflik yang dihadapi oleh Matt dengan mudah. Semuanya seperti 'been there, done that. Chill bro'. Mungkin kalau gw bacanya di umur yang lebih muda, gw akan melihat buku ini sepenuhnya fiksi. Buku ini memang fiksi sih, semuanya karangan. Tapi hal-hal yang disampaikan itu bener banget. Kalau pun ada yang nggak bener, paling itu karena perbedaan budaya dan pergaulan antar kita orang timur dan Matt Beckford sang orang barat.<br /><br />Quote favorit gw di buku ini...<br /><br />"Terjadi begitu saja bukan?" kata Gershwin. "Kehidupan menjadi sibuk. Prioritas berubah. Kita hanya bisa menyalahkan diri sendiri, sungguh." -hal.162<br /><br />Itu kalimat yang bener banget saat lo menjelang umur 30 puluh tahun :-)</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296730372" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15225906-sankrutyayan" class="left imgcol" title="Sankrutyayan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451714937p2/15225906.jpg" alt="Sankrutyayan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1296730372?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 06, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15225906-sankrutyayan" class="user" title="Sankrutyayan">Sankrutyayan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2185321.Turning_Thirty" title="Paperback 9780340767948" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1296730372">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1588251044743206830">I feel at ease whenever I read Mike Gayle’s books. It is quite satisfying to see people who are as messed up as yourself getting on with life with much humor and ease. It is assuring to have company of fictional characters in the time of need to entertain you with their small lives spanning over 300 pages but living forever in our minds guiding through tough times. Mike Gayle’s books are like Sunday. They are lazy, amusing, entertaining and fresh. We can see a part of ourselves being represented</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1588251044743206830">I feel at ease whenever I read Mike Gayle’s books. It is quite satisfying to see people who are as messed up as yourself getting on with life with much humor and ease. It is assuring to have company of fictional characters in the time of need to entertain you with their small lives spanning over 300 pages but living forever in our minds guiding through tough times. Mike Gayle’s books are like Sunday. They are lazy, amusing, entertaining and fresh. We can see a part of ourselves being represented in various characters of his stories. <br /><br />The start was intriguing. The neighborhood of Matt is fantastic as I imagined it. I have always wanted to grow up in one place with a lot of people around you who know you and can identify you from school and from regular places you go. It is ideal life for me sometimes, having the opportunity to grow up with friends from school. But at the other times when I start pondering upon life and things with consequences, it seems inane to spend your life at one place instead of moving around meeting new people. Now that I have never had a life like I imagined, I am deeply in love with people and places from ‘Turning Thirty’. And on top of that there is a person who is a platonic friend and ex-girlfriend who is jealous on the other side of the Atlantic is quite blissful. <br /><br />Having said all the good points about the book, I want to say that I am not surrounded by people who give a damn about turning thirty and all. Now the book instilled some really strong standards I need to meet when I turn thirty. I can never be normal again, like back to where I do not care about age. Anyway it is a good thing to have plans; I never had any. It seems a long time to thirty even though it is just 8 years. 8 years would have been far too long if I were in my teens or below. But after I turned twenty everything seems to move faster, the time predominantly. Because we realize and remember. <br /><br />Matt –“Sometimes recognition by our peers of a seemingly pointless achievement is all we have to live for.” How accurate and relatable is that. I have always complimented people for their seemingly pointless achievements which they consider are significant. That is the way you make people happy. Those are the things which are remembered for life. Everybody applauds when there is an achievement which is naked to the eye, but friends see the hidden. <br /><br />Here it rained all night and is serene in the morning today when I woke up. This is the book which is just like the weather here. I want to take out my bicycle and want to feel the fresh air and smile at all the people on my way. Mike Gayle seems like a guy who smiles at every person crossing his path and it would be definitely reassuring for them. These books make people happy and at ease. That is why I read books, to feel safe and happy. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1588251044743206830">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1322470046">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1022745368966776560">Mike Gayle has been praised for his chatty style and this is undoubtedly the easiest fictional novel I have read this year. It's quite big at 350 pages, but I read it in less than a week.<br /><br />It reads a lot like chick-lit, despite being written by a man (I wouldn't class it as lad fiction). My main issue is it just didn't seem authentic. Most of the characters are successful, or maybe I can't relate because most people within my world are a failure (including me). The fact the lead character could dr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1022745368966776560">Mike Gayle has been praised for his chatty style and this is undoubtedly the easiest fictional novel I have read this year. It's quite big at 350 pages, but I read it in less than a week.<br /><br />It reads a lot like chick-lit, despite being written by a man (I wouldn't class it as lad fiction). My main issue is it just didn't seem authentic. Most of the characters are successful, or maybe I can't relate because most people within my world are a failure (including me). The fact the lead character could drift from one relationship to another seemed a bit strange as well.<br /><br /> It is nostalgic in two ways: the book references the character's love of 80s music (all obvious shit, Wham, Madonna, Culture Club) and the fact it was written in 2000 (Safeways supermarket is now defunct, the Panda 4x4 car is now a very cool and expensive retro car).<br /><br />It's worth a read, it's just not my cup of vanilla chai.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1022745368966776560">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

His protagonist voice is the smart-mouthed, funny, creative simile evoking that his other books have, but that's not different to the kind of lead character you would find in a Linwood Barclay, or Harlan Coben novel.               <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer326891736">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9342238440713317075">First posted January 2006:<br /><br />Being a little over two years away from the big three oh myself (oh...remember those days...) this book struck a chord with me. Many of Gayle's observations about how one feels as they approach thirty were not only hilarious but also right on the money.<br /><br />Matt Beckford is turning thirty in about 89 days and his life is falling apart! He thought by the age of thirty he would have it all together, the fancy high paying job, the woman who was "the one" to spend his life with</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9342238440713317075">First posted January 2006:<br /><br />Being a little over two years away from the big three oh myself (oh...remember those days...) this book struck a chord with me. Many of Gayle's observations about how one feels as they approach thirty were not only hilarious but also right on the money.<br /><br />Matt Beckford is turning thirty in about 89 days and his life is falling apart! He thought by the age of thirty he would have it all together, the fancy high paying job, the woman who was "the one" to spend his life with and the trendy house complete with the requisite "thirty-people's" wine rack. However, Matt finds himself three months away from his birthday moving out of his live in girlfriend's apartment and back to Birmingham to live with, dare I say it...his PARENTS! Now Matt has to figure out what turning thirty really means and he enlist the help of some of his oldest friends to figure it out.<br /><br />This is the third novel by Gayle that I have had the pleasure of reading and he is definitely a very talented and witty author whose voice has never gotten lost in his stories. As popular as Gayle is in the UK it is surprising that he isn't better known it the US however now with the wide re-release of `TURNING THIRTY' he may just find himself at the top of the US's best sellers list soon.<br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/2185321.Turning_Thirty" title="Paperback 9780340767948" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2642764-sherri-hunter?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer93386427">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9600756119994875988">This was the first Mike Gayle book I have read and it will not be my last. I found the story to be full to the brim of nostalgia and reunion. It reminded me of relationships in my own life that have passed me by. I was reminded how we all change, sometimes for the better, as we get older and that my own "turning thirty" brought out a lot of anxiety in myself.<br /><br />I have to say that my favorite part of this book is the advice that Matt so sagely dispenses:<br /><br />"1. Don't take anything for granted because wh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9600756119994875988">This was the first Mike Gayle book I have read and it will not be my last. I found the story to be full to the brim of nostalgia and reunion. It reminded me of relationships in my own life that have passed me by. I was reminded how we all change, sometimes for the better, as we get older and that my own "turning thirty" brought out a lot of anxiety in myself.<br /><br />I have to say that my favorite part of this book is the advice that Matt so sagely dispenses:<br /><br />"1. Don't take anything for granted because when it's gone it's always too late.<br />2. Look after your mates --- and they will look after you.<br />3. The only thing in life that gets easier the older you get is the ability to fall asleep in the middle of a conversation.<br />4. Never move back in with your parents --- it's always a bad idea.<br />5. And, finally, don't go to the pub unless there's somewhere to sit down.<br />But basically it's all just common sense."<br /><br />I would be interested to see these characters revisited as they approach 40. :o)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_208259021">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208259021" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5721564-utami" class="left imgcol" title="Utami"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1369473256p2/5721564.jpg" alt="Utami" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/208259021?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5721564-utami" class="user" title="Utami">Utami</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11407935-turning-thirty---beranjak-tiga-puluh" title="Paperback 9789792270297" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer208259021">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12548085447387385936">Kayaknya GPU menerbitkan buku-buku Mike Gayle dalam waktu yang bersamaan ya? Dan rata-rata konsep desain sampulnya mirip. Simple, tanpa banyak warna-warni permen tipikal sampul novel chicklit.<br />Matt baru saja putus dengan pacarnya. Dia ditawari posisi baru di tempat kerjanya yang mengharuskan dia pindah ke Australia. Akan tetapi, bukannya langsung berangkat, Matt minta cuti selama tiga bulan untuk pulang ke kota kelahirannya. Dia tinggal kembali bersama orang tuanya, dan bertemu dengan teman-teman</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12548085447387385936">Kayaknya GPU menerbitkan buku-buku Mike Gayle dalam waktu yang bersamaan ya? Dan rata-rata konsep desain sampulnya mirip. Simple, tanpa banyak warna-warni permen tipikal sampul novel chicklit.<br />Matt baru saja putus dengan pacarnya. Dia ditawari posisi baru di tempat kerjanya yang mengharuskan dia pindah ke Australia. Akan tetapi, bukannya langsung berangkat, Matt minta cuti selama tiga bulan untuk pulang ke kota kelahirannya. Dia tinggal kembali bersama orang tuanya, dan bertemu dengan teman-teman lamanya.<br /><br />Bagi saya, buku ini seperti sebongkah pengalaman hidup Matt selama tiga bulan. Saya tidak menangkap konflik utama yang benar-benar muncul dalam buku ini. Kita dibawa mengikuti bagaimana Matt menemui teman-teman lamanya, menyaksikan betapa waktu benar-benar dapat merubah seseorang. Sebagian teman-teman lamanya menjadi seperti apa yang telah diramalkan sejak dulu, sementara sebagian lagi menjadi orang yang tak pernah dibayangkan Matt sebelumnya. Jadi ya membacanya berasa agak flat aja. Seperti membaca suatu monolog dari Matt. I don’t feel that the main character is engaging enough.<br /><br />Selain soal menghadapi perubahan teman-temannya, Matt juga dihadapkan pada hubungan percintaannya yang aneh antara dia, Elaine mantan pacarnya, dan Ginny, teman lamanya yang dulu juga pernah menjadi pacarnya. Jadi mungkin salah satu hal yang cukup menarik dalam buku ini adalah menebak-nebak, akhirnya si Matt lebih memilih Elaine, atau Ginny.<br />Tema utamanya sebenarnya cukup familiar dan membumi. Aren’t we all like Matt? Wondering what happened with the people that used to be around us?<br /><br />Kurangnya buku ini ya itu tadi. Flat. Saya tidak bisa menangkap karakter apapun yang menonjol dari tokoh dalam buku ini. Semuanya terasa sama saja. But still, at least setelah membaca buku ini saya jadi terpikir, that maybe it would be nice to have the kind of reunion that Matt had with his friends =).<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12548085447387385936">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer403518343">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12987341292641844368">I love how Mike Gayle writes. Turning Thirty is the second book he's written that I loved reading. He writes as though he were simply having a conversation and the fact that his characters are just ordinary people trying to live their lives and make meaning of all of it is simply delightful.<br />I noted three things about Mike's writing: his characters talk about music, they hang out with friends and connect with their families and they email each other. These were common in both Turning Thirty and D</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12987341292641844368">I love how Mike Gayle writes. Turning Thirty is the second book he's written that I loved reading. He writes as though he were simply having a conversation and the fact that his characters are just ordinary people trying to live their lives and make meaning of all of it is simply delightful.<br />I noted three things about Mike's writing: his characters talk about music, they hang out with friends and connect with their families and they email each other. These were common in both Turning Thirty and Dinner for Two.<br /><br />But, Turning Thirty follows the life of Matt Beckford who wants to make meaning of his life as he turnes 30-and having broken up with his girlfriend Elaine, and gotten a transfer to Sydney he feels as though moving back in with his parents in Birmingham would give him time to meet his high school friends and see how they clocked thirty and what they have achieved. He also hopes to make meaning of his on-off status with Ginny-which I was disappointed didn't happen but what he did after all that is still something worth reading.<br /><br />I loved this book because of how realistic it is. There is no hero or heroine- but just ordinary people living their lives and making the best of it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12987341292641844368">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12110341535740458009">This book was alright. I originally planned to read this book a few months ago in "preparation" for my own 30th birthday, but didn't end up getting to it until the day after. This was a fast read and sometimes an entire page (and chapter) consisted of a one paragraph email. I liked the writing style of this book for a nice change of pace though.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText12110341535740458009">This book was alright. I originally planned to read this book a few months ago in "preparation" for my own 30th birthday, but didn't end up getting to it until the day after. This was a fast read and sometimes an entire page (and chapter) consisted of a one paragraph email. I liked the writing style of this book for a nice change of pace though. I found the short chapters to be very accommodating when I was trying to squeeze a chapter or two in around other things. <br /><br />The story itself was pretty superficial and you really didn't even get to know the main character all that well, much less the supporting characters. Of all the characters, I felt I got to know, and like, Elaine the best which was weird b/c she's supposed to be his ex-girlfriend but she continues to play a pretty major role in his life even after they break up.<br /><br />In my opinion, if you're about to turn 30, or recently have, then you will enjoy this story enough by relating to many of the emotions and changes he's going through at this juncture in his life. If you're not in that category I would pass on this book as there isn't enough plot and character development there to keep you interested.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15277415206926680802"><br />Aspects of this book were fun for their true-isms, aspects of it were confusing because they didn't follow "the formula" where all other pointers suggested they would. <br /><br />The most complex thing about it (now, anyway) is the way it reads like a period piece, accidentally emphasising how different the concerns of the pre-university fees, jobs-everywhere generation were from the turning thirty generation of now. The entitlement is so inherent in that generation, it isn't even addressed, it's just part</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15277415206926680802"><br />Aspects of this book were fun for their true-isms, aspects of it were confusing because they didn't follow "the formula" where all other pointers suggested they would. <br /><br />The most complex thing about it (now, anyway) is the way it reads like a period piece, accidentally emphasising how different the concerns of the pre-university fees, jobs-everywhere generation were from the turning thirty generation of now. The entitlement is so inherent in that generation, it isn't even addressed, it's just part of that age. In a sense, it makes it more dull than it might be now, or perhaps, to say the other way, it's hard to accept a story without any grit in it. <br /><br />And given that it isn't even meant to be so much gritty and plot-driven as it is a light reflection - this certainly isn't trying to be Generation X, and thank goodness, because I don't want to throw it at the wall for that - it isn't that I want a book from twelve years ago to account for this or anything, it's that I don't feel it's aged in a way that gives it the easy fun that it must have had in it at the time. I'd pick up other novels by the author, but with a hope that they wouldn't leave me with the uncomfortably creeping nostalgia of this one...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8209613712155828348">Gostei bastante do livro. Apesar de não ter trinta anos e de ainda me faltarem 4 para lá chegar achei-o...reconfortante. Eu própria passei por uma mini-crise de idade o mês passado quando fiz os 26.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText8209613712155828348">Gostei bastante do livro. Apesar de não ter trinta anos e de ainda me faltarem 4 para lá chegar achei-o...reconfortante. Eu própria passei por uma mini-crise de idade o mês passado quando fiz os 26. Não queria sair dos 25 altura em que ainda somos jovens (pelo menos é o que o Estado diz já que só temos cartão jovem até aos 25 e só pagamos bilhete jovem nos teatros e exposições até aos 25). Porque assim mostrava que tinha aprendido algo.<br /><br />Talvez um livro para reler daqui a 4 anos quando estiver à beira de virar os trinta...<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/18489412-justin-newman" class="user" title="Justin Newman">Justin Newman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/469920.Turning_Thirty" title="Paperback 9780743477659" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer588512553">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18370412305061485596">Reading Mike Gayle is like viewing the new Twilight films: you know what you're getting into. His writing is fun, light, and quick. I read these types of books when Spring comes around to lighten up my mood, since I tend toward the heavier volumes when it is cold out. <br /><br />But, just like the Twilight saga (or the Hunger Games or whatever has replaced Twilight), there are a lot of flat characters in here. The dialogue is snappy and sometimes witty, but tends to fall a bit flat also. The conflicts all</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18370412305061485596">Reading Mike Gayle is like viewing the new Twilight films: you know what you're getting into. His writing is fun, light, and quick. I read these types of books when Spring comes around to lighten up my mood, since I tend toward the heavier volumes when it is cold out. <br /><br />But, just like the Twilight saga (or the Hunger Games or whatever has replaced Twilight), there are a lot of flat characters in here. The dialogue is snappy and sometimes witty, but tends to fall a bit flat also. The conflicts all seem to fall into place a bit too easily, and the few truly deep moments are glossed over to get to a drastic funny moment (or an action sequence in the case of the films).<br /><br />This doesn't upset me because I take these types of things for what they are. I like laughing out loud while reading and Gayle usually gets me to guffaw obnoxiously at least once per book (twice in this one). I can tear through the dialogues in less than two days most of the time, and I always leave his books feeling a little happier than I was before. <br /><br />So as long as you don't over-dissect this book (or any of Mike Gayle's books) and read it for entertainment, you will have a good time. And if you are seeking a deep piece of modern fiction then why in the world are you reading a book that says "A Warm, Funny Romantic Comedy" on the front cover? I shake my head at the bad reviews this guy gets. <br /><br />He does what he does well, and what he does is find the humor in the everyday and give clever new insight to that which plagues us all: relationships. Not Shakespeare, but it's not supposed to be. Read it and smile.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18370412305061485596">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2250856406049997484">Light reading and funny. Might as well fall into "chick-lit" category.<br />Read it a bit too early when I was 25 which is five years ago. I am trying to remember why I was interested in this book:<br />- the main character was a computer programmer who was contemplating his life when the turned thirty.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText2250856406049997484">Light reading and funny. Might as well fall into "chick-lit" category.<br />Read it a bit too early when I was 25 which is five years ago. I am trying to remember why I was interested in this book:<br />- the main character was a computer programmer who was contemplating his life when the turned thirty. I was, kind of, doing it when I turned 25 :-)<br />- although not set as a "serious, philosophical" novel, it might as well evoke philosophicalish thoughts in me regarding time and age. I was then reading popular physics books on cosmology, universe, etc. Time plays a major role in this discussion. <br /><br />Now I can actually say that turning thirty is not that bad. It is even calmer and more down-to-earth. You have known better about who you are and what you want in life. Hehehe... kind of! At least better than when I was in my 20s. You know better what challenges to take since you know better what you are capable of. In contrast to the 20s when you feel you can do and be anything you want. You were just invincible againts the whole world. I love my twenties, and looking forward to more adventures in my thirties. <br /><br />Hopefully that was the message from the author. Pardon me if I am wrong, I read it five years ago, you know! </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_6657714">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6657714" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/352711-leftbanker" class="left imgcol" title="Leftbanker"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1387706300p2/352711.jpg" alt="Leftbanker" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/6657714?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 27, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/352711-leftbanker" class="user" title="Leftbanker">Leftbanker</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/469920.Turning_Thirty" title="Paperback 9780743477659" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/352711-leftbanker?shelf=novels" class="actionLinkLite">novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6657714">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12933669225606756605">I am reading the Spanish translation of this book, <em>Al Borde del los Treinta</em>, which is the only reason I'm giving it all of those damn stars. It is a good learning tool for me in Spanish so it deserves the stars. As far as the book goes, I have some problems.<br /><br />I think that it is total bullshit that people make these age milestones out to be anything at all. All age means is how many times you have been around the sun. If the earth's orbit somehow changed or slowed down, would you be any different?</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12933669225606756605">I am reading the Spanish translation of this book, <em>Al Borde del los Treinta</em>, which is the only reason I'm giving it all of those damn stars. It is a good learning tool for me in Spanish so it deserves the stars. As far as the book goes, I have some problems.<br /><br />I think that it is total bullshit that people make these age milestones out to be anything at all. All age means is how many times you have been around the sun. If the earth's orbit somehow changed or slowed down, would you be any different? <br /><br />I have yet to come across a single poignant observation in the book. The protagonist, like the story, is pretty unimaginative. He is turning 30 soon so he decides to go live at home with his parents? I'm on page 93 tonight and I thought it would be interesting to begin the review at this point in my reading. 93 pages? Not bad for me in Spanish for one afternoon. I'll back.<br /><br />A day later:<br /><br />It’s difficult for me to believe that the idea of turning 30 was compelling enough for Mike Gayle to write <em>Turning 30</em>. It seems more like something he phoned in as part of a contractual agreement. Turning 30 seems like one of those made-up milestones in life. It seems even less trivial to me than turning 21, a date that meant nothing to me because, although I looked extremely young, I had a bullet-proof fake ID and was able to get into bars since I was 18 or so. I can’t even remember thinking about turning 30. Nevertheless, Gayle seems intent on making this birthday into a sort of Hallmark Defining Moment.<br /><br />The tale begins with the narrator telling us how great his life is: a British ex-patriot living in New York with a good job, his own apartment, and a girlfriend. He quickly and painlessly dispenses with these benchmarks of a successful almost-30-year-old single male, so quickly, in fact, that he hardly bothers with a reason. He takes a sabbatical from work and returns to England to stay with his parents which seems like just the thing any normal person would want to avoid.<br /><br />His parents seem less-than-thrilled upon his unannounced arrival and a bit unwelcoming in his idea to spend a few months with them. Describing your thoughts on turning 30 is a bit of a cliché and the author fuels this cliché with a lot of other minor clichés, like describing his mother’s obsession with cooking and food. Why would any young person who is anything but destitute choose to live with his parents for such a long time, especially if they are the type who still scold their children for staying out all night? I wouldn’t have tolerated that at 17 after I first moved out on my own.<br /><br />He even talks about people in his peer group a few months older than he, thus who have already achieved the status of being 30, as if they are truly different people than those who haven’t, as if he expects to finally grow a penis or be blessed with a real interest in girls.<br /><br />I don’t know where he is going with the book as I am only on page 183 of 341, and I don’t know if I plan to stick around to see if he chooses to go or say anything insightful (he hasn’t thus far). I wouldn’t have read this far if I weren’t reading it in Spanish, so it is a learning tool on that front, if nothing else.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12933669225606756605">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17745566901940628512">Really like this novel... Hmmm, baca 3 buku novel karya Mike Gayle, langsung klik "become a fan" doi di GR ini...<br /><br />Ceritanya tentang Matt Beckford yang bakal berulang tahun ke 30 tanggal 31 Maret. Udah mapan, kerja di New York dan punya pacar Elaine, umur 22. Ehhh, entah kenapa, pas bulan Januari, si Elaine mutusin Matt. Gara gara ini, si Matt jadi minta pindah kerja dan balik ke Birmingham sono buat ngisi cuti 3 bulannya...<br /><br />Di Birmingham, Matt terpaksa tinggal di rumah ortunya. Udah gitu, Matt mencoba untuk ngehubungin 6 orang sahabatnya selama sekolah di Birmingham itu... Ketemu sih, bahkan sempet reunian juga. Buntutnya, si Matt malah naksir naksiran lagi ama Ginny Pascoe, salah satu sahabatnya itu... Si Ginny ini dari jaman baheula emang -selain sahabat- juga temen kencannya si Matt kalo lagi ga ada pacar. Mereka bahkan bikin perjanjian kalo sampe umur 30 mereka berdua gak punya pacar, yasud, mereka bakal pacaran.<br /><br />Sementara di Inggris, si Matt tetep email email an ama Elaine sang mantan pacar. (Enak yaaa, bisa tetep sahabatan ma mantan pacar...). Bahkan si Elaine sampe datang ke England dan nginep di rumah ortunya Matt buat ngerayain ultah ke 30 nya Matt.<br /><br />Trus, apa yang terjadi di ultah ke 30 nya Matt? Baca sendiri aja yaaa...<br /><br />Ngomongin 30 tahun... This August I'll be 35 years old... Pas mo menjelang 30 tahun, kek nya daku nggak ngalamin kehebohan yang dialami si Matt deh... Biasa aja gitu, gak kepikiran seperti pikiran si Matt Beckford...</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LUvHLbVjZ8jnnTYG5bTT8zBJrgGk4U91h6LTM1nVjOdIn/j+R7FzMmtFQr2b1TVBeb5tGO08CN/tq9ahlUB6og==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EG/w4R8I4LqAohkRmYe0Noa7WO7xIiS45gN8avtqXxt1u88y7dr0QAx6barn5lKEz0yb97j/YxKMCnn4N/+pXg==')})
  }

Han er 13 år gammel, og vet at gitaren må bli hans. Han har 43 kroner på konto og gitaren koster kr. 2250. En ny verden åpner seg da han får jobb som blomsterbud hos Finsens Flora på Frogner.           $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_466782').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_466782').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_466782').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script>
</li>
</ul>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/46977.Mike_Gayle">About Mike Gayle</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/46977.Mike_Gayle"><img alt="46977" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1266386567p2/46977.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer16555063967927409561">I was born in the 70s — the 70s were great. I would recommend them to anyone.<br /><br />I was also born in Birmingham — in my humble opinion the greatest city in the world with the nicest people too.<br /><br />I used to live in London — a great city too. But a bit on the pricey side.<br /><br />I also used to live in Manchester — another great city (although technically I lived in Salford which is next door but that’s sort of spli</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16555063967927409561">I was born in the 70s — the 70s were great. I would recommend them to anyone.<br /><br />I was also born in Birmingham — in my humble opinion the greatest city in the world with the nicest people too.<br /><br />I used to live in London — a great city too. But a bit on the pricey side.<br /><br />I also used to live in Manchester — another great city (although technically I lived in Salford which is next door but that’s sort of splitting hairs).<br /><br />Before I went to university I wanted to be a social worker — I have no idea why. It didn’t last long.<br /><br />After I left university I wanted to write for the NME — I’ve always loved music but it was only when I went to uni that it started loving me back. I can’t play any instruments or sing so writing about music seemed to make sense.<br /><br />My first paid writing gig was for a listings magazine in Birmingham — (Actually my first unpaid writing gig was an interview with Kitchens of Distinction for Salford Student Magazine. I can’t begin to tell you how terrible it was.)<br /><br />I used to write a music fanzine — it was called Incredibly Inedible and I co-edited it with my mate Jackie. We typed up the first issue on my dad’s olde worlde typewriter and then literally cut and paste on to A4 sheets using scissors and glue. Over the three years of its existence we interviewed many bands and artists including: Smashing Pumpkins, The Cranberries, Pavement, Bill Hicks and Blur.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16555063967927409561">...more</a>
